  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f342aca1-dca1-4f88-afce-caa221ff5527'
      });
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13400833233320821788"><i>This is the final battle.</i><br/><br/>The Alliance is losing the war, and their most critical weapon, seventeen-year-old witch Nathan Byrn, is losing his mind. Nathan’s tally of kills is rising, and yet he’s no closer to ending the tyrannical rule of the Council of White Witches in England. Nor is Nathan any closer to his personal goal: getting revenge on Annalise, the girl he once lov</span>
  <span id="freeText13400833233320821788" style="display:none"><i>This is the final battle.</i><br /><br />The Alliance is losing the war, and their most critical weapon, seventeen-year-old witch Nathan Byrn, is losing his mind. Nathan’s tally of kills is rising, and yet he’s no closer to ending the tyrannical rule of the Council of White Witches in England. Nor is Nathan any closer to his personal goal: getting revenge on Annalise, the girl he once loved before she committed an unthinkable crime. An amulet protected by the extremely powerful witch Ledger could be the tool Nathan needs to save himself and the Alliance, but this amulet is not so easily acquired. And lately Nathan has started to suffer from visions: a vision of a golden moment when he dies, and of an endless line of Hunters, impossible to overcome. Gabriel, his closest companion, urges Nathan to run away with him, to start a peaceful life together. But even Gabriel’s love may not be enough to save Nathan from this war, or from the person he has become.<br /><br />Set in modern-day Europe, the final book in the Half Bad trilogy is more than a story about witches. It’s a heart-achingly visceral look at survival and exploitation, the nature of good and evil, and the risks we take for love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13400833233320821788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389165463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5446685714089180576">Now <b>THAT</b> is how you end a series. Wow. This book destroyed me. I admit I had some reservations after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_' title='Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'> Half Wild</a>, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7314532.Sally_Green' title='Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'> Sally Green</a> redeemed herself and ended this series the way it deserves. I'm at such a loss for words. I need some time to gather my thoughts.<br/><br/>Okay, I think I can write this review now. When I say this book destroyed me, I 100% mean it. The feels I was feeling can’t even be explained. I laughed, cried, cheered, screamed, cried some more, smiled, cried a hell of a lot more, and on i</span>
  <span id="freeText5446685714089180576" style="display:none">Now <b>THAT</b> is how you end a series. Wow. This book destroyed me. I admit I had some reservations after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_" title="Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Wild</a>, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7314532.Sally_Green" title="Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sally Green</a> redeemed herself and ended this series the way it deserves. I'm at such a loss for words. I need some time to gather my thoughts.<br /><br />Okay, I think I can write this review now. When I say this book destroyed me, I 100% mean it. The feels I was feeling can’t even be explained. I laughed, cried, cheered, screamed, cried some more, smiled, cried a hell of a lot more, and on it goes. I can’t think of any other series that has ended in a way that has had me this satisfied. Everything was addressed. The beauty of it is that there were things set up in the previous books that I didn’t even see coming! I guess this more than makes up for what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_" title="Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Wild</a> lacked. If you wrote the series off at that point, pick it back up. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814993.Half_Lost__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___3_" title="Half Lost (The Half Bad Trilogy, #3) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Lost</a> has the same excitement that filled the pages of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_" title="Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Bad</a> making it unputdownable.<br /><br />Two months have passed since the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_" title="Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Half Wild</a> and Nathan is hell-bent on getting his revenge. The Alliance of Free Witches has suffered a great loss, but is still fighting for the cause they believe in - a world where both the Black and White witches can live together peacefully. The corrupt Council and Hunters are both still trying to end the existence of Black witches, half-codes, the Alliance, and most importantly Nathan. Neither side will back down. Get ready for an intense fight to the end!<br /><br />There are romance developments in this one that explore a ship I’m sure others are both anxious and excited to see. It is done in a beautiful way and don’t want to say anything else about it.<br /><br />The character development over the course of the series was fantastic! From the moment we met some of the characters in the first book (or even the second), with all the things they have gone through- as expected- they’ve grown in more ways than way. I’ve enjoyed this journey with the characters and loved seeing the way everything turned out for them.<br /><br />Aside from the fact that by the end of this book I was surrounded by tissues trying not to destroy the pages I had just read with my tears...this was a GREAT read. The entire series made me feel so many things bringing plenty of twists and surprises along the way. I can’t wait to see what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7314532.Sally_Green" title="Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sally Green</a> does next!<br /><br /><b>I received an ARC in exchange for an honest review from PenguinTeen.</b></span>

<div id="review_1296096834" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296096834" />
    <a title="Maggi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16969868-maggi"><img alt="Maggi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453844797p2/16969868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296096834?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggi" href="/user/show/16969868-maggi">Maggi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1296096834&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296096834" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17336959293656156189">Oh! See how this book was on the shelf <i>need-more-than-my-next-breath</i>! Now see how it's going straight into the trashcan! Also, see how I am tempted to lower the rating to one star!<br/><br/>Honestly, I'm not sure whether to even write this review, because it will be next to incomprehensible and not as much a review as a rant about how fucking done I am with this book. Enjoy! (Seriously, this is nothing but an angry rant and sarcasm. Also every second word is fuck, so beware.)<br/><br/>The reason I started this tril</span>
  <span id="freeText17336959293656156189" style="display:none">Oh! See how this book was on the shelf <i>need-more-than-my-next-breath</i>! Now see how it's going straight into the trashcan! Also, see how I am tempted to lower the rating to one star!<br /><br />Honestly, I'm not sure whether to even write this review, because it will be next to incomprehensible and not as much a review as a rant about how fucking done I am with this book. Enjoy! (Seriously, this is nothing but an angry rant and sarcasm. Also every second word is fuck, so beware.)<br /><br />The reason I started this trilogy was an amazing post on tumblr telling me about all the diverse characters, canon bi and gay soulmates!, and I definitely can't resist that in an universe with modern day witches.<br />And I loved the first two books! The character development was super well done and I couldn't wait to see how the story ends. Sally's tweets and tumblr posts convinced me we would get a fantastic ending. But ha, how wrong I was. I'm 97% sure she was on drugs writing the last 50 pages.<br /><br />Not only did the ending make 0,001% sense, Green basically punched us all in the face. Diversity? How good is that even if the gay kid gets killed off again and the other one turns into a fucking tree?<br /><br />JFC. Fuck this whole book and everything it stands for.<br />For a moment tonight I thought "Well, I do understand why she ended it the way she did." but fuck no, I do not understand and <b>I refuse to understand</b> why you have to kill off another LGBTQ+ couple / mess their lives up (and fucking turn one into a tree, ha, what a good joke lmao, Sally stop it :'-)) in YA literature.<br /><br />What was the point of this ending? Is there even a fucking point? <br />The only thing I can come up with is that she wanted to show how war can mess someone's life up. But who the fuck here doesn't know how messy war can be? We've read about Nathan's struggle, we saw him getting worse page after page, his emotional state showed us perfectly well how horrible the situation was. Why the fuck was it necessary to kill off the person he loves the most? His fucking soulmate? Hasn't he been through enough already? <b>Nathan deserves so much better</b>.<br />And so fucking does Gabriel. His death didn't make any sense and didn't serve any other purpose than to mess Nathan's life up. So what, this time it isn't the typical '<i>let's kill this LGBTQ+ character to contribute to the straight character's development</i>' but a '<i>ha let's kill a gay character to completely ruin the life of a bisexual character, ha, what a great idea</i>'? Dear Sally Green, what the fuck?<br /><br />Nathan survived getting locked up in a fucking cage, was bullied and abused, lost his family and was used as a weapon in a war when he was 17. I repeat, <b>seven-fucking-teen</b>. HE WAS A FUCKING CHILD. So what do we do with him? Kill off the last bit of life-joy he has and turn him into a tree. Bravo! What a twist! <br /><br />I have one last thing to say. Fuck you. Fuck you for killing of another teenager LGBTQ+ couple, we definitely haven't witnessed it enough. <br /><br /><br /><br />.........a motherfucking tree, jfc. what drugs was she on. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1602624318?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602624318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17413477592836839311">I'm so angry at this book, and not because it was sad, and not because I always want a happy ending (I don't), and not because I think that in order for a book to be good it has to have a happy ending. That's not the case at all. <br/><br/>I'm so angry at this book because it felt like the entire thing was just window dressing for the Shocking Ending. And I know that anyone who thinks the ending was ridiculous and pointless and depraved is going to be accused of wanting "rainbows and unicorns" but guess f</span>
  <span id="freeText17413477592836839311" style="display:none">I'm so angry at this book, and not because it was sad, and not because I always want a happy ending (I don't), and not because I think that in order for a book to be good it has to have a happy ending. That's not the case at all. <br /><br />I'm so angry at this book because it felt like the entire thing was just window dressing for the Shocking Ending. And I know that anyone who thinks the ending was ridiculous and pointless and depraved is going to be accused of wanting "rainbows and unicorns" but guess fucking what: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am sick and tired of reading, and watching, stories about LGBTQIAP people dying tragically or suffering alone. You can sit there and say, "Tons of straight people died in this book" and that's true, yes they did, but (a) killing off all queer characters and/or leaving them to live miserable and alone forever is such an aggressively common trope in media that has significant cultural weight, and (b) scores of straight people (and almost all of them White witches!) went off and lived peacefully and moved on from the war. Meanwhile, exactly 0 queer people had happy endings. You have a gay boy dying in his lover's arms and then a bisexual boy killing himself by turning himself into a tree.<br /><br />I'm not okay with this, and nor am I okay with this book being really flat and lacklustre, filled with battle strategy that I couldn't follow, filled with Nathan fucking hating himself forevermore and never being allowed to heal either from losing Gabriel or from his war trauma or from the abuse he suffered in his teenage. Do not tell me that "well, it's a war book" because we've had shitloads of war books that have been painfully, epically sad and horrible and yet have not ended with this ridiculous shock value ending. Why kill Gabriel off? Why leave this protagonist to suffer for years before ultimately ending his own life at the age of twenty-two? If this had been an adult book, it still would have been problematic, but much less so. But you're writing a war book for teens, so don't pretend that there isn't any morality at all between these pages.<br /><br />So what is this book saying? There's no way to recover if you're broken. Forget it. Fuck life. Or, if you're broken and straight, you might be all right, but if you're broken and queer, you can FORGET ever being happy again. But the thing is that I didn't sign on for that shitty pointless soapbox finale, and neither did I sign on to consume <i>another</i> piece of media that ends with more sad, dead queer people. I'm fucking sick of it and when I cried at the end of this, they weren't, "Oh, I'm so sad but enjoying this" tears, they were "I'm so sad and furious and there is no hope here, there is nothing but hatred, nothing to take away from it, nothing at all". <br /><br />Van's death adds to this in that she was coded as gender non-conforming and yeah, of course, she died too. "Yeah, but it's war". Yeah, but you sent boatloads of cis, hetero characters off to live in peace while the only queer characters died. "Yeah, but that's war". Yeah, but finding a decent well-written fantasy book with queer protagonists has 1000-1 odds. Finding a decent well-written fantasy book with ANY queer characters is pretty rare in itself, so when you then kill off all of those queer characters, who's fucking left? "Yeah but it's a war book." Yeah, but this is a fictional account of it. You have control over it, and symbolism is something that you create. There is no symbolism in the real world, but novels are full of it. It's the whole point of them. <br /><br />Look at the <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> series: heartbreaking. Absolutely devastatingly sad. But it didn't rely on killing off the only marginalized characters for shock value. In fact, almost all of the main characters survived. Did that make it less shocking? No. Did that make it less sad? No. <br /><br />Look at <i>The Hunger Games</i>: the representation of queer people was non-existent, but then again, there was precious little time for anything but straightforward plot. And it was also devastatingly sad, so honest and open and frank about the cost of war, and yet our protagonists didn't end up slumping down and giving up. They were not destroyed by their trauma.<br /><br />What do we look for in war novels? Do we look for messages of bloodshed, of violence, of the awful darkness in humanity? Why do we look for that? What's the point in reading war novels just to revel in how fucking dreadful people can be to each other? A war novel that champions hope in the face of incredible adversity, that reminds us of the good that people can do even when they'd been compelled to do bad, and that speaks of the light at the end of the tunnel, is infinitely more compelling than a war book that throws its characters into a meat grinder and then does nothing with it. I'm not asking for a book about how everything always works out fine after a war, essentially preaching that war is necessary, no - I'm looking for a book like <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> that rejects war completely, that presents peace as always being the better option, that speaks of the total senselessness that is organized violence. Karou said to her people, "What do you see in our future?" and that is what makes that series so brilliant in the way that it handles war. It doesn't ask whether or not war is necessary, and it doesn't scream "Yeah, I'm super gritty" and it doesn't annihilate its only marginalized characters just to show off how Super Dark it is. It rejects the idea of war altogether and illustrates how absolutely pointless it is.<br /><br />I loved the first two books in this series, because it seemed like this was the direction they were going. Waking up to how peace is the only way to move forward. The characters felt so real to me, and Nathan's voice was so strong, and I was so connected to it. But this brilliant protagonist who had survived being locked in a cage, mutilated, emotionally and physically abused, and ostracized by society was reduced to <i>sad, just sad</i> in <i>Half Lost</i>. <br /><br />I'm just so angry about this. And it's not even all about the Kill Your Gays trope. It's about the waffling storyline, the confusing action, the total lack of a satisfying ending. There's about half a sentence of resolution for every major character we've been following over the course of the series and I actually could not believe that it cut off where it did: unresolved, unfinished, absurdly depressing and mopey.<br /><br />I'm still crying about this but they aren't cute tears. They're fucking irritated tears. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Basically, this book was a massive letdown and I'm not happy about it in the slightest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17413477592836839311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2545120572785797738"><u>
  <b>READ #2, November 2017:</b>
</u><br/>I'M BROKEN AND EVERYTHING HURTS AND WHY THE HECK DID I WANT TO REREAD THIS. This book gave me anxiety. Also I freaking love it. I love this whole series. It is brutal and actually really cleverly told (the foreshadowing is A+ the whole way through) and it actually underlines the physical and psychological damage of war. <b>The characters are <i>real</i>, so so real</b>. I didn't read this book...I fell into it. The powerful writing, the agony, the triumph, the wildness and the broke</span>
  <span id="freeText2545120572785797738" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>READ #2, November 2017:</b>
</u><br />I'M BROKEN AND EVERYTHING HURTS AND WHY THE HECK DID I WANT TO REREAD THIS. This book gave me anxiety. Also I freaking love it. I love this whole series. It is brutal and actually really cleverly told (the foreshadowing is A+ the whole way through) and it actually underlines the physical and psychological damage of war. <b>The characters are <i>real</i>, so so real</b>. I didn't read this book...I fell into it. The powerful writing, the agony, the triumph, the wildness and the brokenness have completely swallowed me whole.<br /><br />I love it, ok. I truly love this trilogy. Also the pureness of Gabriel and Nathan is &lt;3<br /><br />(Please bring me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34508382.The_Smoke_Thieves" title="The Smoke Thieves by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Smoke Thieves</a> soonnnnn.)<br /><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>READ #1: April 2016</b>
</u><br />This book actually <b>BROKE ME INTO 1000000 PIECES AND I SHALL NEVER BE OKAY.</b> I don't even know how to word right now. SOMEONE JUST LEAD ME TO A QUIET FIELD WHERE I SHALL STAY FOR ETERNITY IN MY BROKENNESS.<br /><br />Okay but honestly: <b>it was perfect.</b> And I love this series. It is the most best and underrated series of my LIFE. Seriously, ever since I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_" title="Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Bad</a>, I kind of suffocated under the realisation that this was raw, beautiful genius. The writing inspires me. Nathan is the most REAL character I've read in 3948398 years. (Um, yeah, I've lived that long. In <i>book years</i>, okay?) I get so choked up reading these books. I want to re-read them a million times. I want to just hold them and protect them because THEY ARE MIIIIIIIINE. <br /><br />(PS I am broken.)<br /><br /><b>This book is a lot shorter than the others.</b> And it is the perfect length. There is so much less weird-wacky formatting though? I liked how the formatting reflects Nathan and how he's maturing and changing. Buuuut I <i>did</i> miss it, because it's one of the biggest reasons I liked bk 1 so much.<br /><br />But.<br /><br />It was perfect. <br /><br />AM I rEAPEATING mYSELF? whY Is tHAt yOU aSK? BeCAUSE mY MinD DOeS NoT worK.<br /><br /><b>And of course Nathan and Gabriel are forever my FAVOURITE.</b> This is a ship that I have not shipped quite so aggressively in a long time. I JUST. I LOVE THEM. And Nathan is <i>nasty</i> in this book and Gabriel doesn't just take it (which I love) and I was so so worried and then I was so so happy and then I was so so -- um. Ahem. I shall not tell you my finale emotions.<br /><br />Also I appreciate how Nesbit is the biggest Nathan/Gabriel shipper out there:<br /><blockquote>"Is Gabriel still mad at me?"<br />"Nesbitt hesitates and then says, "On a scale of one to ten, I'd say he's at nine and a half."<br />"So, it could be worse then."<br />"He'll calm down." Nesbitt nudges me and says, "The best thing about arguments is the making-up after. I see a big reconciliation ahead for you two: you apologise and he takes you into his arms and --"<br />"Nesbitt, shut up."</blockquote><br />I SHIP THEM TOOOOOO NESBITT. (Wait is it Gathan or Nabriel?)<br /><br /><b>I just loved reading it so so much.</b> Every time I put it down; I WANTED TO PICK IT BACK UP.<br /><br />THIS SERIES HAS STOLEN MY HEART.<br /><br />Oh shush everything, <b>I need to talk spoilers:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I KNEW GABRIEL WOULD DIE. I FREAKING NEW IT. THE SECOND MY SHIP SAILED I KNEEEEEEW HE WOULD DIE BECAUSE THIS SERIES IS MERCILESS. And tbh, I've always been able to predict this series because it's really similar to how I write/tell stories (doooon't get me wrong; my writing is watermelon seeds compared to this genius). So I knew that I would let Gabriel die. SO I KNEW IT WOULD HAPPEN HERE AND IT DID. And it was horrifying. And I choked up. Do you realise how often I cry in books? NEVER. AND HERE I AM. A MESSSSSSSSSSSSSS. <br />And then Nathan turned into a tree over his grave. <br />I...I am ridiculously okay with this.<br />I can't BrEATHE.<br />(I'm surprised Nathan/Analisse had a kid though? I honestly can't remember them sleeping together, but I guess the did earlier in the series and I just blocked it haha. #Awkward. Anyway Nathan's kid is Edge and he never met his father. I suppose he could meet a tree but it ain't the same.)<br />And I'm <i>assuming</i> the person who narrates the last chapter is Celia??? Idek why they didn't say her name. THEY COULD'VE SAID HER NAME AND SAVED MY BRAIN TWITCHING.<br />I am a mess. I am a freaking bloody mess right now, I cannot even with this precious book.<br /><b>I loved Gabriel and Nathan so so much.</b><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>I cannot recommend it fiercely enough. <b><br /><br /><br />*** QUOTES ***<br /><br /><blockquote>"The only thing necessary for the triumph of evil is that good men do nothing."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>He says, "You know I love you. Still. Forever."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"You've been away a long time. Were you lost?" He sounds lost himself...<br />"Wounded, not lost," I tell him, but I do feel lost.</blockquote></b></b></span>

<div id="review_1595240957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1595240957" />
    <a title="Leon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13219646-leon"><img alt="Leon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596604810p2/13219646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1595240957?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leon" href="/user/show/13219646-leon">Leon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13219646-leon?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1595240957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2684287388250193175"><p>This review is NOT spoiler free – please proceed at your own peril.</p><br/><p>Let me count the ways I feel so betrayed.</p><br/><p>Some people may remember me a staunch support of this series in its youth. This is the series that got me <i>into </i>YA literature. It was never perfect, but it was interesting and different.</p><br/><p>Instead book three comes out and everything crashes and burns. The plot loses itself (what the hell is blue? Why was it introduced so late?) the characters we’ve become invested in disappear or die (Arran is</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2684287388250193175" style="display:none"><p>This review is NOT spoiler free – please proceed at your own peril.</p><br /><p>Let me count the ways I feel so betrayed.</p><br /><p>Some people may remember me a staunch support of this series in its youth. This is the series that got me <i>into </i>YA literature. It was never perfect, but it was interesting and different.</p><br /><p>Instead book three comes out and everything crashes and burns. The plot loses itself (what the hell is blue? Why was it introduced so late?) the characters we’ve become invested in disappear or die (Arran is <i>barely </i>in this book and Van gets only about a chapter of mourning after her death – and Ellen? <i>She dies off-screen and we get a single passing mention</i>?) and the ending, is, quite bluntly, <i>a fucking disaster. </i></p><br /><p>Honestly, I have read messages in my alphabet soup that spelt out more compelling stories than Sally Green writes.</p><br /><p>But let’s put aside plot talk – because I’m not even gonna pretend to understand that trainwreck – and get to the crux of the matter here.</p><br /><p>In her infinite wisdom, after months and months of baiting the fans and pages and pages of promising a happy ending, <i>she slaughters her lead characters. </i></p><br /><p>Let me repeat that for those of you who don’t understand. She <i>shoots</i> Gabriel, a canonically gay character, at the very last minute so Nathan, her bisexual lead character and Gabriel’s lover, can watch him die in his arms. The bloodbath doesn’t end there though – because now that Gabriel’s gone Nathan lives a few years of intense, traumatized misery (you could say he goes back to his <i>roots </i>I guess) and then he –</p><br /><p>
  <i>Turns into a motherfucking tree. </i>
</p><br /><p>Oh yes. Yes he does. He becomes a fucking tree. All so he “be one with nature” and “watch over Gabriel for eternity” or some other bullshit. Let me say, by the way, Nathan’s ability to turn into anything <i>but </i>animals was not brought up in the entire of the series until this super convenient moment.</p><br /><p>I just. I can’t with this. Why? At what point did Sally Green think this would make sense, narratively speaking??</p><br /><p>But, as gay girl always looking for some representation, I was <i>ecstatic </i>when I found these books. These are books in which the main character is openly bisexual, has a gay love interest and yet the story is very much <i>not about that</i> – it’s everything I wanted.</p><br /><p>And the way Sally posited about on social media, the promise of a future she sowed into her books, I was so sure that for once, just for once, these gay teenagers would get their happily ever after – that for once <i>I would not have to consume another piece of media where me and others like me got slaughtered by a straight writer for the angst of it all. </i></p><br /><p>And then she did it. She did it good.</p><br /><p>I spit on this series now. I loved it so much, I promoted it to all the people I knew, many of whom were gay themselves, I was so excited – I talked with her about it, other people I know talked to her about it, we told her how happy we were to have this sort of representation, and she smiled and lied to her faces knowing all the while what she was going to do.</p><br /><p>So Sally Green, fuck you and fuck your supreme addition to the every growing “bury your gays” trope and I hope you cop the social media backlash you deserve for this.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="2684287388250193175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_906993929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906993929" />
    <a title="mith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7621359-mith"><img alt="mith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586053966p2/7621359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906993929?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mith" href="/user/show/7621359-mith">mith</a>
      </span>

          marked it as maybe-read

<span id="freeTextContainer4605398241982185825">Lmao, Green sure had fun jerking us around. When in doubt, queerbait! <br/><br/>Even better if you can do it personally by interacting with your LGBT readers on your twitter: promise them a happy LGBT ending! Watch them buy your book! Then see them talk about wanting to kill themselves because of how your plotline made them feel and take no accountability!<br/><br/>This book was such a "ride". Because y'know, what a revolutionary ending, one more dead gay kid and one more abused bi kid who don't get a happy ending.</span>
  <span id="freeText4605398241982185825" style="display:none">Lmao, Green sure had fun jerking us around. When in doubt, queerbait! <br /><br />Even better if you can do it personally by interacting with your LGBT readers on your twitter: promise them a happy LGBT ending! Watch them buy your book! Then see them talk about wanting to kill themselves because of how your plotline made them feel and take no accountability!<br /><br />This book was such a "ride". Because y'know, what a revolutionary ending, one more dead gay kid and one more abused bi kid who don't get a happy ending. Maybe some day I'll be able to be objective about this. Maybe some day I'll write a proper review. But honestly, it was deplorable how you acted, Sally Green, how you gave young lgbt readers - young abuse survivors who related with Nathan, hope that he would come out of his struggles alright, happy, healthy and <i>alive</i>. <br /><br />You already stabbed us once, you didn't need to twist the knife in deeper. Eat my ass out.</span>

  <span id="freeText15349994587418201952" style="display:none">[spoilers] <br />Why precious Gabby ;( now every happy scene hurts. Such a tragic love story<br />Always so hopeless.When they finally got together&amp;dared to have one simple dream it was snatched away too. But at least both were free of cruelty &amp; together in tragic peace at the end.<br />Proof for Gabriel's &amp; Nathan's undying love for each other. Like the ring, forever.<br />Their love was so real&amp;mature,actions not just words,love not just empty lust.Respect,loyalty and devotion.<br />Tragic war kids with one simple dream they shared,hold onto to survive,brutally snatched away last second,when it was over.That's why both didn't make it.<br />I wanted all whites to pay. Kill them all like Marcus said. They were dicks. But in the end most got away with everything after making blacks' lives hell for years,even at the camp treating like tools and using slurs to describe them. Nat who suffered so much because of them was threatened with cage, she never paid for torturing&amp;keeping him there. Anna ruined everything and sickeningly simply excused herself, got happiest ending. Gab who was so good&amp;never harmed, loved, and stayed for Nat got killed. Nat suffered,lost everything and not all paid. After he lost Gab he did not even have strength for revenge anymore.<br />Poor boys.<br />I hated people always controlling Nat... with humiliation,pain,potions...forgetting what he went through,threatening for actions yet nobody else was&amp;no one was paying for his pain.Hated the "equality" scene,glad he went against it,but at the end ended up so broken he didnt even care anymore.<br /><b>Where was fairness? <br />Nat&amp;Gab deserved happiness after everything,not the dicks&amp;cowards,those who ran away,hurt,we barely knew.Bullshit not equality&amp;justice.</b><br />Im mad that Nat who didnt really have a choice, &amp; Gab who stayed for him even though he wanted to leave,both who suffered&amp;sacrificed so much,worked so hard for their dream,happy ending,to live together peacefully after war, never got it &amp; nobody paid for their suffering.Fought for the better future when they could just left. While Anna who done no good, worked against them, hurt Nathan, let her brothers torture him, murdered his father who could possibly have saved Gab, never worked for happiness, EXCUSED herself, got the happiest ending imaginable and others, just not Nat, forgave her.<br />WTF? Why he paid for loving?<br />Such a stab.<br />And with that Nat's last sanity, Gab his dream, gone. "Lucky" lived to see Wales unlike him, but...Only the thought of him saved him at the council but then he pretty much died with him. The fact that he waited to change into a tree proved he wanted to do it forever, not change first thing out of desperation to come back when healed. I loved Nat's reaction to Gab's death. This is how it was meant to be esp as Gab would't have died if not him. He knew Gab only stayed because he loved him. &amp; died. The guilt&amp;sacrifice&amp;love were real.<br />Gab died, knowing their dream wont ever come true, there will be no Wales, he won't ever see them, be with Nat after everything was finally starting to seem possible. He was so happy... &amp; deserved it so much for everything he did. It was heartbreaking.<br /><b>I don't get hurting those who fought and gifting those who did not or worse.</b><br />Im grateful that if Gab had to die then Nat's reaction was the one written beginning when he was looking for him. Gab was everything to him and that's it.<br />But he &amp; Gab deserved their happy ending.<br />Nat knew he &amp; Gab'd had more time before, Gab'd have survived &amp; they'd have been happy after war if not Nat, if he listened to Gab. Killed her, didn't waste TIME with/for her hurting&amp;using him to save her. Left the war:Marc&amp;Gab would have survived. They both were in it only for Nat. Saving Anna killed Mar&amp;Gab. Sparing his sister killed Gab. Taking Amulet saved Nat but killed Gab in result. Gab was completely sacrificed. If they just left the war like Gab wanted to...<br />I think that was part of why Nat completely broke. Gab&amp;Marc sacrificed themselves for him out of love &amp; died because of his choices. She who only hurt him survived. Heartbreaking. But he fulfilled his promise &amp; then went after Gab &amp; that made it bearable.<br /><br />I hope it was Nat's bad dream/vision again. Gab just woke him up &amp; they went for a walk &amp; swim in Wales where they live as planned in peace&amp;love. &amp; they spend time by the fire, Nat watching happy Gabby like he wanted,both watch the gorgeous view,love,don't starve anymore,&amp;laugh,swim,hike,sunshine on their pretty now healthy faces,&amp;then travel too, &amp;are just so happy in love together both living their dream... Like they dreamed. Love only growing stronger.<br /><br />I loved Gab not letting Nat treat him bad,Nat feeling bad "how could I?I dont want to ever hurt him again",hating that Gab thought he doesn't care,apologising&amp;working for forgiveness.The ring scene!Finally.<br /><br /><b>They only had one dream. They were each other's dream.</b><br />I'm so heartbroken and emotionally drained.<br />Glad Nat was too. But I just can't accept that the sunshine of the story is dead. It's not how it was meant to end. Poor war kid, he just wanted to live in peace. He was so sacrificing,pretty&amp;cheerful&amp;good,loved but stood his ground,wanted to live,be with Nat with who he just&amp;finally pretty much married,go Wales like promised,leave the war tired of suffering,scared of them dying,but ended up staying out of love &amp;dying in agony for Nat who survived. Never lived to see Wales,be happy.Only his body was taken there.Just when they thought it was over...A second of relief.Fusing.Happiness snatched away suddenly,poor Gabby trying to hold on,Nat scared,desperate holding his hands,him,begging,screaming,kissing,hugging,loving... "you won't die" "dont leave me":( both suffered got ruined completely<br />I was happy that Nat never got over it, it was too much&amp;he followed him.<br /><b>They deserved happiness the most after only suffering so hopeless. They were teased, the visions, hopes, promises... Beyond anything<br />If anybody deserved a happy ending it was them. <br />His death was only accepted by me because the other suffered so much because of it.<br />But it still hurt. Just like Gab's love for him when he fought for his heart, stayed and risked his life, died for Nat.</b>Nat gave him his life too.<br />Nat couldn't heal &amp; Im glad. But he did. And lived there by his grave, when the grass grew over it, never wanting to leave, no matter how much others tried. (They pissed me off. Leave them alone! Boys only had each other) And did not let others pull him away from him. He just found a way to be with him again forever.Securing him.There, where promised, till the end, beyond it. <br /><br />That it happened after a few years, made the love even more real, because you knew he did not do it out of simple desperation right after his death[he chose to grieve first as unbearable as it was], so you'd think he would come back after he would feel better, but no, he said he will wait, and he did it after he calmed a little, but <b>never got over it, he healed enough to not be in denial anymore, to not have them give him potions, but he never accepted it, the agony was still there</b>,he thought everything through with Gab never stopping being his priority,only love,he practiced,thought that through earth they became one when they were looking for the gift so it would be the same when he would change, and how Gab would love to have a tree by him... And Nat did it. Gave him more than a tree. Himself. Basically found a way to hold his hands again. <br />After a few years he still only wanted him.Still most important.Nat's love for Gab won &amp; he joined him just as he planned in the very beginning. From the moment he realised his love, it only grew stronger&amp;nothing managed to break it. After a few years he did it as planned and that's how we know it was forever, not temporary. <br />It was beautiful. <br /><br />Gab dying&amp;Nat never moving on but finding a way to be with him again was a happy ending in its own way. It was about their unconditional true love at the end, death could not change it, love Nat luckily returned, late but not too late. At least they could spend some time together before everything went to hell. Gab knew Nat loved him, he proved plenty, I'd hate if he died not knowing. Nat moving on, leaving, wouldn't be a happy ending to me. Because he would break the promise and leave when Gabriel never did. Besides I really believe he could not realistically heal. The tree full of bruises said it all. He lost too much. <b>Gab was the last person who held him sane. Was always meant to. And then was taken away from him too. [Nat desperately holding, hugging his dead body. Gosh... I can't believe he died.] When everything started falling into place... They were making plans for the future...</b> And I appreciate he wasn't "exchanged" for someone else. It'd be sick.<br /><br />They found their "peace" together,even if in the most tragic way. Exactly where they wanted to be,Nat found a way to be with his soulmate against all, ignoring others telling him to accept and move on. Gab would not leave either.Nat screamed love since he realised he really feels it for Gab. He wanted to apologise for everything [Love that Gab stood his ground and did not let Nat treat him badly] and make up for it, bringing Gabby to tears. When he gave him the ring... Sincere thoughts&amp;worry for him were precious. And after everything he mentally broke&amp;never gave up but finally found his way to him. Their relationship wasn't based on lust but love in the first place (that's why it won over the emptiness that was A/N).<br />The innocent precious love they had for each other made the ending even more heartbreaking.They suffered enough but it never got better for them, only worse.<br /><br />I was terrified of Nat moving on with Anna, it would be the biggest stab in the back especially after Gab died for him. He wanted to leave but stayed for him. And died killed by his sister.<br />Or even with the other magician... It just wouldn't feel right. This one just wanted him for himself. Gab &amp; Nat were meant to be together in Wales. That was the plan, the promise - Nat kept it. Others trying to change his mind made me want to shoo them away. Nat was the only one who truly cared about Gab, the only family. The ring... it was practically engagement and when he said Gab will keep it forever... It was a promise, engagement,marriage-it was important. He promised him Wales and he took him there and stayed with him forever even after death. He fulfilled his promise even though Gab never lived to see Wales with his own eyes. And just being there wasn't enough, he found a way to basically hold his hands again.<br /><br />I am happy that if one had to die, the other kind of did too, wanted to be with him,found a way. It was all beautiful in its cruel way. More if they both just died. Because they proved their unconditional love for each other.<br />I would prefer if they fulfilled their dreams, they would be in Wales happy &amp; alive just like they were meant to be, just like Nat could not stop seeing it, like they deserved &amp; clung to the dream, and I wanted to be in denial too, but if I could not have them alive... <b>at least it were Wales, because Nathan promised him Wales, and they stayed together, just as he promised him too. Against others trying to make him move on. <br />Nathan never left Gabriel, he found a way to be with him forever even after his death.<br />Their love was beautiful. </b><br /><br /><b>"wounded, not lost" Nat's last words, their password</b>, showing how he never forgot and never managed to get over Gab's death because it was too much&amp;he loved him beyond anything. He finally found a way to be with Gab again. The whole idea of him staying with him even after death... keeping him safe, never wanting to leave, was so touching. Finding a way to hold his hands again. So right.<br />Poor kids :( They were tragic war kids who deserved so much better. Hurts that those undeserved did instead.<br />Remember when they've met? :( Their love won with everything, even with death at the end, but it was too short when they were alive. I wish Anna was never in the way, that she died not Gab, that Nat wouldn't have wasted time when they were still alive. I wish he left with Gab when there was still time. He never forgot himself for not doing it and saving him, them, in result.<br /><br />For a moment I thought they saved Gab. Like Nat, living in denial too, but his reaction to his death was 'perfect'. It showed how much it broke him so how much he loved him. <br />They deserved happiness beyond anything,not to be broken completely after everything they went through. Together happy in Wales, finally the kids they were meant to be, keeping each other safe.ALIVE.They repeated so many times how much they wanted it. <br /><br />I just wish the ending said "i read to them"</span>
  <a data-text-id="15349994587418201952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1554875855" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1554875855" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554875855?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554875855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15128977364064241486"><blockquote>
  <i>“I’ve killed fifty-two people. But really all I want is to get my hands on her. I’d be happy with fifty-three. Just one more and I’ll be satisfied."</i>
</blockquote><br/>2 1/2 stars. I liked this book more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_' title='Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Half Wild</a>. I liked the gay romance. I liked that Nathan is a true antihero with a murderous mean streak that he actually acts upon - in other words, he isn't just one of those characters who's sold as an antihero but never does anything questionable.<br/><br/>But I have a theory. The same theory I have about series </span>
  <span id="freeText15128977364064241486" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“I’ve killed fifty-two people. But really all I want is to get my hands on her. I’d be happy with fifty-three. Just one more and I’ll be satisfied."</i>
</blockquote><br />2 1/2 stars. I liked this book more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_" title="Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Wild</a>. I liked the gay romance. I liked that Nathan is a true antihero with a murderous mean streak that he actually acts upon - in other words, he isn't just one of those characters who's sold as an antihero but never does anything questionable.<br /><br />But I have a theory. The same theory I have about series like Ee's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>: the author came up with a fascinating and exciting premise - good witches! bad witches! magic! misunderstandings! inner struggle between good and evil! - and then lost it when it came time to turn that premise into a compelling story arc.<br /><br />I really loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_" title="Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Bad</a>. Not everyone did, but I thought the writing and the idea were instantly engaging. I enjoyed reading about how Nathan grew up as a problem kid and everyone expected the worst of him because his father was a black witch - and, in the end, was it nature or nurture that made him the way he was? The story was realistically frightening and unfair.<br /><br /><b>But that story started to wander in circles in both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814989.Half_Wild__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___2_" title="Half Wild (The Half Bad Trilogy, #2) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Wild</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814993.Half_Lost__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___3_" title="Half Lost (The Half Bad Trilogy, #3) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Lost</a></b>. I lost count of how many times Nathan's inner narrative repeated his feelings about his father and how alike they are, his feelings about Annalise and how he must find her, and his feelings about Gabriel. <br /><br />The plot itself also moves in a pattern of:<br />1) Find the bad guys<br />2) Infiltrate bad guys hideout<br />3) Kill bad guys<br /><br />As I said, I enjoyed this book more than the last one, but I still find myself looking back over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20814993.Half_Lost__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___3_" title="Half Lost (The Half Bad Trilogy, #3) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Lost</a> and wondering what it really contributed to the series and story. There is literally one "big" and memorable occurrence near the end and, truth be told, it was just kind of disappointing. <b>This is a very real spoiler:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[we finally get a central gay romance in YA fantasy and the author kills off the gay love interest? It just leaves a bad taste. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This isn't even a case where the story feels dragged out longer than necessary... rather, it feels like the author wrote it with no idea where it was going. It doesn't really seem to have a climax and the ending kind of fizzles out.<br /><br />If you read and enjoyed the first two books, then it makes sense to read this finale and get your closure. But if you've been skeptically raising an eyebrow for a while now, you're honestly not missing much.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15128977364064241486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1499433864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499433864" />
    <a title="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm"><img alt="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423864239p2/24060858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1499433864?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" href="/user/show/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm">Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1499433864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6133492869071969953">**** I'd probably suggest not reading this review if you haven't read Half Wild yet, as it spoils the end of Half Wild! ****<br/><br/>I both loved and hated Half Lost. Okay, okay... I LOVED IT! But I am a broken human being right now. I am hurt deep in my soul and don't know what to even do about it. Sally Green definitely knows how to write an epic finale that can shock and surprise her readers, and happily crush our hearts and souls. Prepare yourself for this book, it is going to be a book you find impo</span>
  <span id="freeText6133492869071969953" style="display:none">**** I'd probably suggest not reading this review if you haven't read Half Wild yet, as it spoils the end of Half Wild! ****<br /><br />I both loved and hated Half Lost. Okay, okay... I LOVED IT! But I am a broken human being right now. I am hurt deep in my soul and don't know what to even do about it. Sally Green definitely knows how to write an epic finale that can shock and surprise her readers, and happily crush our hearts and souls. Prepare yourself for this book, it is going to be a book you find impossible to put down.<br /><br />Nathan begins the book angry as all hell. He has an absolute hatred for Annalise that he will not get over. He wants revenge for his fathers death, his one mission seems to be hunting her down and killing her. And, I'm sorry.... I DON'T GET IT! Seriously, I need someone to properly explain this to me as I still don't see why he suddenly hates Annalise. Okay, yes, she did kill his father, which did result in a large number of the Alliance dying. But, she did this because she was shooting his father as he was slitting her brothers throat. I'm sorry, in this instance, I am on Annalise's side. Nathan swore no harm would come to him, but his father stood there and quite happily shoved a knife into his throat. He should have known Annalise wasn't just going to stand by and watch. Connor was the only member of her family she loved, the only one who treated her well. She grew up with him and cared for him. Nathan has known his father for five bloody minutes. I'm sorry, Nathan, get over it! You have way better things to worry about right now, leave it alone. I felt it was just a convenient way to get Annalise out of the picture and allow the Nathriel ship to sail - not that I am complaining about that.<br /><br />Gabriel is still my favourite part of this series, I adore that boy so much. I wish he was a real character because he would be my new best friend. I LOVE HIM! And I love him with Nathan. This book just set my shipper heart racing like nothing else, these two are just two freaking cute!<br /><br />There is a lot going on in this book. The Alliance are trying to work to take down the Council and the Hunters and work out a way for Black and White witches to live together peacefully. There is a lot of action in this book and it is a book you are going to find so hard to put down. I couldn't get enough of the book, but I definitely feel like the Half Wild is still my favourite, mostly because it didn't reduce me to a useless, blubbery mess. I cried so hard during the ending of this book, I hurt just thinking about it.<br /><br /><br /><br />5/5 Butterflies<br /><br />Part of me wants to know points off the book just for the fact it made me cry harder than a book has managed to do in years. But I can't. Okay, it broke me, but it ended beautifully. Sally Green gave us an incredible and action-packed finale. She made my shipper heart happy and she gave me twists, turns and shocks. I feel so sad having to say goodbye to this series and its characters, but I will be eagerly awaiting whatever Sally Green writes next. <br /><br />For those who have read this... BIG SPOILER.... SO PLEASE ONLY READ IF YOU HAVE READ. OR DON'T CARE HAHA <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Can we just talk about Gabriel dying please?!?! I AM STILL DEVASTATED. WHY WOULD GREEN DO THAT TO US!?!?!!!!! Ahhhhh it still hurts.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1597510907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1597510907" />
    <a title="Cee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54500968-cee"><img alt="Cee" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1597510907?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cee" href="/user/show/54500968-cee">Cee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597510907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13225590484336537979">*spoilers*<br/><br/>I am so very, very disappointed with this book. <br/><br/>Sally Green threw away a great premise, wonderful characters, by writing the same, dreadful tropes. <br/><br/>Do you know how hard it is to find Lgbt+ books? Do you know how hard it is to find good Lgbt+ books that don't focus on sexuality? It's a thousand to one. It's a thousand to one, and none of the Lgbt+ characters ever get a happy ending. <br/><br/>I cannot believe that Sally used social media, made it very clear that she was marketing this book to you</span>
  <span id="freeText13225590484336537979" style="display:none">*spoilers*<br /><br />I am so very, very disappointed with this book. <br /><br />Sally Green threw away a great premise, wonderful characters, by writing the same, dreadful tropes. <br /><br />Do you know how hard it is to find Lgbt+ books? Do you know how hard it is to find good Lgbt+ books that don't focus on sexuality? It's a thousand to one. It's a thousand to one, and none of the Lgbt+ characters ever get a happy ending. <br /><br />I cannot believe that Sally used social media, made it very clear that she was marketing this book to young, Lgbt+ teens, and then she goes and kills of the two lgbt+ protagonists, whilst the minor straight (white, able bodied, neurotypical) characters carry on and live a fulfilling life<br /><br />The deaths don't even serve any purpose, they didn't further the plot at all. The war was won. It's pure wangst. To make the characters suffer. To have another tragic story that's been done a thousand times before.<br /><br />And of course everybody's telling us to shut up - people kill their characters all the time! It's dramatic, gritty realism! Stop whining about your precious Gay Characters dying.<br /><br />Listen. For every one tragic story with a straight romance/character that ends in tragedy there are a hundred ones with happy endings. Plenty of representation. You can find another. They are everywhere.<br /><br />Lgbt+ teens don't have that luxury. What little representation either ends in tragedy, or ends in heartbreak. They can't pick up another book and find their happy ending. <br /><br />All you're doing is depriving 15, 16 year olds - scratch that, 14 year olds, 12 year olds, - of their much needed representation. The media doesn't cater to them. And you can't taunt them with happy endings, with characters they can relate to, and then just ruin it all.<br /><br />Do you know what message that's sending to these kids? The group of people most likely to commit suicide? The ones with next to no representation at all, who face discrimination regularly, who'll always be treated differently?<br /><br />You don't get a happy ending.<br /><br />Bury your tropes, not us. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13225590484336537979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1145962579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1145962579" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1145962579?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1145962579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16160276654458043840"><i>
  <blockquote>“I’m tired of your revenge, your anger, your hate. The war is killing you.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><b>This trilogy should have been a standalone. Or a duology.</b><br/><br/>Firstly, I need to establish - I LOVED the first book. I thought <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_' title='Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Half Bad</a> was awesome and atmospheric and gritty. The sequel was pretty good too, though in my opinion this trilogy peaked at the end of the first book.<br/><br/>I hated <i>Half Lost</i>. Everything I loved from the previous books was gone and it had everything that annoyed me - boring writing, a plot that went nowh</span>
  <span id="freeText16160276654458043840" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“I’m tired of your revenge, your anger, your hate. The war is killing you.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><b>This trilogy should have been a standalone. Or a duology.</b><br /><br />Firstly, I need to establish - I LOVED the first book. I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18079804.Half_Bad__The_Half_Bad_Trilogy___1_" title="Half Bad (The Half Bad Trilogy, #1) by Sally Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Bad</a> was awesome and atmospheric and gritty. The sequel was pretty good too, though in my opinion this trilogy peaked at the end of the first book.<br /><br />I hated <i>Half Lost</i>. Everything I loved from the previous books was gone and it had everything that annoyed me - boring writing, a plot that went nowhere, clichés, and irritating characters. The main problem I had, though, was with the main character.<br /><br />This was pretty much Nathan's train of thought for the entire book:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Later I remember what I could do. It’s easy. I could kill them all.”</blockquote>
</i><br />What I loved about Nathan in the first book was the dark sadness that surrounded him - he was a half Black, half White Witch and an outcast. He was excluded and beaten for no reason other than his lineage. But in this book he lost all of that and was consumed by a single thought: <b>KILL KILL KILL.</b><br /><br />The first 250 pages (out of a 350-page novel) were building up for the ending. And when it finally came, it was just a series of quick action scenes and pointless violence.<br /><br />Also, I thought it was really cheesy how Nathan practically became invincible. With all of his new, special Gifts he was pretty much immortal. So when he ran into battle - the "climax" of this book - I was stifling a yawn. Like, I know those guys he's fighting can't touch him, so I'm bored.<br /><br />Nathan's hatred-filled narration was exhausting. Within the first thirty pages, I was done listening to him yammer on and on about Annalise and the Alliance and his father. I honestly didn't care.<br /><br />What makes me so sad is that this trilogy had such a strong start, but this final book was a complete disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16160276654458043840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319944595" />
    <a title="Mai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12295071-mai"><img alt="Mai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477760638p2/12295071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1319944595?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mai" href="/user/show/12295071-mai">Mai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12295071-mai?shelf=books-in-my-room">books-in-my-room</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1319944595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17624784456920123084">Okay, so I've calmed down although I still have tears streaming down my face as we speak.<br/><br/>This might be the best book of the whole trilogy yet it was the worst one of them, it was the most beautiful thing ever yet the most tragic of them all. Looking at the story throughout the three books, I think that Nathan had the worst life ever, the most unfair everything and none of what'd happened to him was his fault.<br/><br/>I fell in love with this book and the writing with every page I turn, the way the story </span>
  <span id="freeText17624784456920123084" style="display:none">Okay, so I've calmed down although I still have tears streaming down my face as we speak.<br /><br />This might be the best book of the whole trilogy yet it was the worst one of them, it was the most beautiful thing ever yet the most tragic of them all. Looking at the story throughout the three books, I think that Nathan had the worst life ever, the most unfair everything and none of what'd happened to him was his fault.<br /><br />I fell in love with this book and the writing with every page I turn, the way the story took its path, the way it was written, the way the characters were developed, how the romance reached its peak, all was good and jolly.<br /><br />Some books will break your heart, and some books will just end it for you, and other will boost your happiness. This is one of the books who can do all of that, this is one of the books who can be everything you want yet everything you run away from.<br /><br />Sally Green tells an amazing story, a tragically marvelous one, and it breaks my heart that it's come to an end as she had found a way to attach the character to my heart, and I wouldn't want to let go, I took my time to read this book because I didn't want it to end, I wanted it to go on forever.<br /><br />You know how sometimes you adopt the characters and you feel overly protective of them? I just felt that throughout the whole book, so this is one of the reasons why the book broke me. But looking at the bigger picture now, this ending was so realistic, and I accept it after a whole day of being in a state of denial. The story is greater this way, it's carved into my heart. The romance was the most beautiful thing ever.<br /><br />I just can't talk about this book and not spoil so I'll just stop right here, and say that I'll always love this book and I will read my first couple of chapters whenever I'm sad or down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17624784456920123084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2028600820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2028600820" />
    <a title="☙ nemo ❧" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19742661-nemo"><img alt="☙ nemo ❧" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604079632p2/19742661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2028600820?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☙ nemo ❧" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☙ nemo ❧" href="/user/show/19742661-nemo">☙ nemo ❧</a>
      </span>

          marked it as nein-nein-nein




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=blacklist">blacklist</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2028600820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11036639212550760699">hahHAHAHA fuck this book and fuck the author <br/><br/>(this is going to contain spoilers so Beware)<br/><br/>i'm not averse to tragic endings in general and neither am i averse to tragic endings in queer books (although i generally avoid them because we get enough tragedy in our day-to-day lives); i'm not gonna be all THIS BOOK SUX BC THE GAYS DIED <i>necessarily</i>. <br/><br/>the thing that is disgusting and the reason why i'm not gonna fuckin read this book is because she was queerbaiting her (mostly lgbt, mostly teenage fans) </span>
  <span id="freeText11036639212550760699" style="display:none">hahHAHAHA fuck this book and fuck the author <br /><br />(this is going to contain spoilers so Beware)<br /><br />i'm not averse to tragic endings in general and neither am i averse to tragic endings in queer books (although i generally avoid them because we get enough tragedy in our day-to-day lives); i'm not gonna be all THIS BOOK SUX BC THE GAYS DIED <i>necessarily</i>. <br /><br />the thing that is disgusting and the reason why i'm not gonna fuckin read this book is because she was queerbaiting her (mostly lgbt, mostly teenage fans) asking them to send in fanart of main M/M pairings and posting excerpts of the happy ending of the m/m couple but it turned out it was a huge lie and she killed them off. <br /><br />it's pretty stupid to do something like that <i>regardless</i> of queer content; i find that pretty unprofessional actually. it's not a Huge Twist or a "haha, got you!!" moment, it's just fucking pathetic.. add that to the charged cultural backdrop of queer teens being delighted that queer characters get a happy ending for once, only for it to turn out that <b>they fucking die after all,</b>and it's just horrible. to my knowledge, she hasn't yet apologised, and until she does, i won't be reading anything else by this author. <br /><br />i haven't rated this book and i don't intend to, and before anyone Starts, the widespread discontent and anger amongst her fanbase shows that this isn't just a couple of "special snowflakes" getting their feelings hurt, it's a group of LGBTQ fans being <b>deliberately misled</b> which leads to irritation and disappointment on the part of the reader, because they wanted to read a book where a queer person like them got a happy ending and they fucking didn't. <b>the author strung them along to get publicity and sales for her book and then lied.<b><br /><br />fuck. honestly the worst case of "bury your gays" to EVER, EVER exist. </b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11036639212550760699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
